Rule Generator Message:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing a carboxylic acid group (-COOH) and an aromatic ring tend to result in a high yield. This is likely due to the ability of the carboxylic acid to coordinate with the metal center, enhancing the stability and reactivity of the catalyst. Examples include 4-(bromomethyl)benzoic acid and 4-aminobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with an amino group (-NH2) and a linear aliphatic chain of 4 to 6 carbons tend to result in a high yield. The amino group can enhance coordination with the metal center, while the aliphatic chain may provide steric effects that favor the reaction. Examples include 5-aminopentanoic acid and 7-aminoheptanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a hydroxyl group (-OH) and an aromatic ring tend to result in a high yield. The hydroxyl group can participate in hydrogen bonding, potentially stabilizing the catalyst structure. Examples include 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid and 2-oxo-1H-pyridine-4-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple ether linkages (-O-) tend to result in a low yield. The presence of ether linkages may lead to increased flexibility and decreased rigidity in the catalyst structure, which can negatively impact the reaction. Examples include 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers containing a sulfanyl group (-SH) tend to result in a high yield. The sulfanyl group can provide strong coordination with the metal center, enhancing the catalytic activity. Examples include 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a nitro group (-NO2) on an aromatic ring tend to result in a high yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the nitro group can stabilize the metal center, enhancing the reaction. An example is 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (-CF3) tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the trifluoromethyl group may destabilize the metal center, reducing catalytic activity. An example is 4-[(2,2,2-trifluoroacetyl)amino]butanoic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers containing an indole group tend to result in a high yield. The indole group can provide π-π interactions and additional coordination sites, enhancing the stability and reactivity of the catalyst. An example is (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

**End of Rules**

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[c]'],  # Rule 1: Carboxylic acid and aromatic ring
        ['[NX3H2]', '[C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4]'],  # Rule 2: Amino group and aliphatic chain
        ['[OX2H]', '[c]'],  # Rule 3: Hydroxyl group and aromatic ring
        ['[OX2][CX4][OX2]'],  # Rule 4: Multiple ether linkages
        ['[SX2H]'],  # Rule 5: Sulfanyl group
        ['[NX3+](=O)[O-]', '[c]'],  # Rule 6: Nitro group on aromatic ring
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 7: Trifluoromethyl group
        ['c1c[nH]c2c1cccc2'],  # Rule 8: Indole group
        ['c1ccncc1'],  # Rule 9: Pyridine ring
        ['[CX3H]=O', '[c]']  # Rule 10: Formyl group on aromatic ring
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 4, 5, 8]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Rules with low prediction
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1][c]'],  # Rule 1: Carboxylic acid directly attached to aromatic ring
        ['[NX3H2]', '[C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4]?'],  # Rule 2: Amino group and aliphatic chain of 4 to 6 carbons
        ['[c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 3: Hydroxyl group directly attached to aromatic ring
        ['[OX2][CX4][OX2]'],  # Rule 4: Multiple ether linkages
        ['[SX2H]'],  # Rule 5: Sulfanyl group
        ['[c][NX3+](=O)[O-]'],  # Rule 6: Nitro group directly attached to aromatic ring
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 7: Trifluoromethyl group
        ['c1c[nH]c2c1cccc2'],  # Rule 8: Indole group
        ['c1ccncc1'],  # Rule 9: Pyridine ring
        ['[c][CX3H]=O']  # Rule 10: Formyl group directly attached to aromatic ring
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 4, 5, 8]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Rules with low prediction
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

Matrix Checker Message:
** Start of Suggestions **

- ** Suggestion 1 **: For Rule 1, the SMARTS pattern '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1][c]' only checks for a carboxylic acid directly attached to an aromatic ring. However, the rule also requires the presence of an aromatic ring, which is not explicitly checked. Consider using a SMARTS pattern that ensures both the carboxylic acid and the aromatic ring are present, such as '[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'.

- ** Suggestion 2 **: For Rule 2, the SMARTS patterns '[NX3H2]' and '[C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4]?' are used. The second pattern is intended to match a linear aliphatic chain of 4 to 6 carbons, but it may not accurately capture this structure. Consider using a more specific pattern like '[C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4]?[C;X4]?' to ensure the chain length is between 4 and 6 carbons.

- ** Suggestion 3 **: For Rule 3, the SMARTS pattern '[c][OX2H]' is used, which correctly identifies a hydroxyl group attached to an aromatic ring. This seems appropriate, but ensure that the aromatic context is correctly captured in all cases.

- ** Suggestion 4 **: For Rule 4, the SMARTS pattern '[OX2][CX4][OX2]' is used to identify multiple ether linkages. This pattern may not capture all possible ether linkages, especially if they are not in a simple linear form. Consider using a more flexible pattern like '[OX2][CX4][OX2]' with additional context to capture variations in ether linkage structures.

- ** Suggestion 5 **: For Rule 5, the SMARTS pattern '[SX2H]' is used, which correctly identifies a sulfanyl group. Ensure that this pattern is applied in the correct context to match the rule's intent.

- ** Suggestion 6 **: For Rule 6, the SMARTS pattern '[c][NX3+](=O)[O-]' is used, which correctly identifies a nitro group attached to an aromatic ring. This seems appropriate, but ensure that the aromatic context is correctly captured in all cases.

- ** Suggestion 7 **: For Rule 7, the SMARTS pattern '[CX4](F)(F)F' is used, which correctly identifies a trifluoromethyl group. This seems appropriate, but ensure that the context of the group is correctly captured in all cases.

- ** Suggestion 8 **: For Rule 8, the SMARTS pattern 'c1c[nH]c2c1cccc2' is used, which correctly identifies an indole group. This seems appropriate, but ensure that the context of the group is correctly captured in all cases.

- ** Suggestion 9 **: For Rule 9, the SMARTS pattern 'c1ccncc1' is used, which correctly identifies a pyridine ring. This seems appropriate, but ensure that the context of the group is correctly captured in all cases.

- ** Suggestion 10 **: For Rule 10, the SMARTS pattern '[c][CX3H]=O' is used, which correctly identifies a formyl group attached to an aromatic ring. This seems appropriate, but ensure that the aromatic context is correctly captured in all cases.

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 1: Carboxylic acid directly attached to aromatic ring
        ['[NX3H2]', '[C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4]?[C;X4]?'],  # Rule 2: Amino group and aliphatic chain of 4 to 6 carbons
        ['[c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 3: Hydroxyl group directly attached to aromatic ring
        ['[OX2][CX4][OX2]'],  # Rule 4: Multiple ether linkages
        ['[SX2H]'],  # Rule 5: Sulfanyl group
        ['[c][NX3+](=O)[O-]'],  # Rule 6: Nitro group directly attached to aromatic ring
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 7: Trifluoromethyl group
        ['c1c[nH]c2c1cccc2'],  # Rule 8: Indole group
        ['c1ccncc1'],  # Rule 9: Pyridine ring
        ['[c][CX3H]=O']  # Rule 10: Formyl group directly attached to aromatic ring
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 4, 5, 8]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Rules with low prediction
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

Current rules:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing a carboxylic acid group (-COOH) and an aromatic ring tend to result in a high yield. This is likely due to the ability of the carboxylic acid to coordinate with the metal center, enhancing the stability and reactivity of the catalyst. Examples include 4-(bromomethyl)benzoic acid and 4-aminobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with an amino group (-NH2) and a linear aliphatic chain of 4 to 6 carbons tend to result in a high yield. The amino group can enhance coordination with the metal center, while the aliphatic chain may provide steric effects that favor the reaction. Examples include 5-aminopentanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a hydroxyl group (-OH) and an aromatic ring tend to result in a high yield. The hydroxyl group can participate in hydrogen bonding, potentially stabilizing the catalyst structure. Examples include 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple ether linkages (-O-) tend to result in a low yield. The presence of ether linkages may lead to increased flexibility and decreased rigidity in the catalyst structure, which can negatively impact the reaction. Examples include 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers containing a sulfanyl group (-SH) tend to result in a high yield. The sulfanyl group can provide strong coordination with the metal center, enhancing the catalytic activity. Examples include 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a nitro group (-NO2) on an aromatic ring tend to result in a high yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the nitro group can stabilize the metal center, enhancing the reaction. An example is 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (-CF3) tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the trifluoromethyl group may destabilize the metal center, reducing catalytic activity. An example is 4-[(2,2,2-trifluoroacetyl)amino]butanoic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers containing an indole group tend to result in a high yield. The indole group can provide π-π interactions and additional coordination sites, enhancing the stability and reactivity of the catalyst. An example is (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can coordinate with the metal center, enhancing the catalytic activity. Examples include pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers containing a formyl group (-CHO) on an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. The formyl group may introduce steric hindrance or electronic effects that destabilize the metal center. Examples include 4-formylbenzoic acid.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

   - For molecules where the predicted loading is high but the experimental value is low, Rule 1 and Rule 5 often have high positive SHAP values, indicating they might be contributing to overestimation.

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing a carboxylic acid group (-COOH) and an aromatic ring tend to result in a high yield. This is likely due to the ability of the carboxylic acid to coordinate with the metal center, enhancing the stability and reactivity of the catalyst. Examples include 4-(bromomethyl)benzoic acid and 4-aminobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with an amino group (-NH2) and a linear aliphatic chain of 4 to 6 carbons tend to result in a high yield. The amino group can enhance coordination with the metal center, while the aliphatic chain may provide steric effects that favor the reaction. Examples include 5-aminopentanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a hydroxyl group (-OH) and an aromatic ring tend to result in a high yield. The hydroxyl group can participate in hydrogen bonding, potentially stabilizing the catalyst structure. Examples include 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple ether linkages (-O-) tend to result in a low yield. The presence of ether linkages may lead to increased flexibility and decreased rigidity in the catalyst structure, which can negatively impact the reaction. Examples include 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers containing a sulfanyl group (-SH) tend to result in a high yield. The sulfanyl group can provide strong coordination with the metal center, enhancing the catalytic activity. Examples include 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a nitro group (-NO2) on an aromatic ring tend to result in a high yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the nitro group can stabilize the metal center, enhancing the reaction. An example is 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (-CF3) tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the trifluoromethyl group may destabilize the metal center, reducing catalytic activity. An example is 4-[(2,2,2-trifluoroacetyl)amino]butanoic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers containing an indole group tend to result in a high yield. The indole group can provide π-π interactions and additional coordination sites, enhancing the stability and reactivity of the catalyst. An example is (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can coordinate with the metal center, enhancing the catalytic activity. Examples include pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers containing a formyl group (-CHO) on an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. The formyl group may introduce steric hindrance or electronic effects that destabilize the metal center. Examples include 4-formylbenzoic acid.

Rule Generator Message:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing a carboxylic acid group (-COOH) and an aromatic ring with electron-donating substituents (e.g., -OH, -NH2) tend to result in a high yield. The electron-donating groups enhance coordination with the metal center, stabilizing the catalyst. Examples include 4-aminobenzoic acid and 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with an amino group (-NH2) and a linear aliphatic chain of 4 to 6 carbons, without additional electron-withdrawing groups, tend to result in a high yield. The amino group enhances coordination, while the aliphatic chain provides steric effects that favor the reaction. Examples include 5-aminopentanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a hydroxyl group (-OH) and an aromatic ring with additional electron-donating groups tend to result in a high yield. The hydroxyl group participates in hydrogen bonding, stabilizing the catalyst structure. Examples include 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple ether linkages (-O-) and no additional functional groups tend to result in a low yield. The flexibility and decreased rigidity of the catalyst structure negatively impact the reaction. Examples include 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers containing a sulfanyl group (-SH) with a short aliphatic chain (up to 3 carbons) tend to result in a high yield. The sulfanyl group provides strong coordination with the metal center, enhancing catalytic activity. Examples include 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a nitro group (-NO2) on an aromatic ring tend to result in a high yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the nitro group stabilizes the metal center, enhancing the reaction. An example is 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (-CF3) tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the trifluoromethyl group destabilizes the metal center, reducing catalytic activity. An example is 4-[(2,2,2-trifluoroacetyl)amino]butanoic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers containing an indole group tend to result in a high yield. The indole group provides π-π interactions and additional coordination sites, enhancing the stability and reactivity of the catalyst. An example is (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring coordinates with the metal center, enhancing catalytic activity. Examples include pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers containing a formyl group (-CHO) on an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. The formyl group introduces steric hindrance or electronic effects that destabilize the metal center. Examples include 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with an aromatic ring and electron-withdrawing groups such as sulfonyl (-SO2-) or carbonyl (-C=O) groups tend to result in a low yield. These groups may destabilize the metal center. Examples include 4-sulfanylbenzoic acid.

**End of Rules**

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[c][OX2H]', '[c][NX3H2]'],  # Rule 1: Carboxylic acid and aromatic ring with electron-donating groups
        ['[NX3H2]', '[C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4]'],  # Rule 2: Amino group and linear aliphatic chain
        ['[OX2H]', '[c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 3: Hydroxyl group and aromatic ring with electron-donating groups
        ['[OX2][C][OX2]'],  # Rule 4: Multiple ether linkages
        ['[SX2H]', '[C;X4][C;X4][C;X4]'],  # Rule 5: Sulfanyl group with short aliphatic chain
        ['[NX3+](=O)[O-]', '[c]'],  # Rule 6: Nitro group on an aromatic ring
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 7: Trifluoromethyl group
        ['c1c[nH]c2c1cccc2'],  # Rule 8: Indole group
        ['c1ccncc1'],  # Rule 9: Pyridine ring
        ['[CX3H]=O', '[c]'],  # Rule 10: Formyl group on an aromatic ring
        ['[c][SX4](=O)(=O)', '[c][CX3](=O)']  # Rule 11: Aromatic ring with sulfonyl or carbonyl groups
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 5, 8]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

- ** Suggestion 9 **: For Rule 9, the SMARTS pattern `['c1ccncc1']` should be verified to ensure it captures the pyridine ring accurately. The current pattern seems correct, but ensure it is applied in the right context.

- ** Suggestion 10 **: For Rule 10, the SMARTS pattern `['[CX3H]=O', '[c]']` should be refined to ensure it captures a formyl group on an aromatic ring. The current pattern may not fully represent the aromatic context.

- ** Suggestion 11 **: For Rule 11, the SMARTS pattern `['[c][SX4](=O)(=O)', '[c][CX3](=O)']` should be adjusted to ensure it captures an aromatic ring with sulfonyl or carbonyl groups accurately. The current pattern may not fully represent the structural context.

** End of Suggestions **

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[c][OX2H]', '[c][NX3H2]'],  # Rule 1: Carboxylic acid and aromatic ring with electron-donating groups
        ['[NX3H2]', '[C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4]'],  # Rule 2: Amino group and linear aliphatic chain
        ['[OX2H]', '[c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 3: Hydroxyl group and aromatic ring with electron-donating groups
        ['[OX2][C][OX2]'],  # Rule 4: Multiple ether linkages
        ['[SX2H]', '[C;X4][C;X4][C;X4]'],  # Rule 5: Sulfanyl group with short aliphatic chain
        ['[NX3+](=O)[O-]', '[c]'],  # Rule 6: Nitro group on an aromatic ring
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 7: Trifluoromethyl group
        ['c1c[nH]c2c1cccc2'],  # Rule 8: Indole group
        ['c1ccncc1'],  # Rule 9: Pyridine ring
        ['[CX3H]=O', '[c]'],  # Rule 10: Formyl group on an aromatic ring
        ['[c][SX4](=O)(=O)', '[c][CX3](=O)']  # Rule 11: Aromatic ring with sulfonyl or carbonyl groups
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 5, 8]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df
---------------------------------------------------------------
Current rules:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing a carboxylic acid group (-COOH) and an aromatic ring with electron-donating substituents (e.g., -OH, -NH2) tend to result in a high yield. The electron-donating groups enhance coordination with the metal center, stabilizing the catalyst. Examples include 4-aminobenzoic acid and 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with an amino group (-NH2) and a linear aliphatic chain of 4 to 6 carbons, without additional electron-withdrawing groups, tend to result in a high yield. The amino group enhances coordination, while the aliphatic chain provides steric effects that favor the reaction. Examples include 5-aminopentanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a hydroxyl group (-OH) and an aromatic ring with additional electron-donating groups tend to result in a high yield. The hydroxyl group participates in hydrogen bonding, stabilizing the catalyst structure. Examples include 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple ether linkages (-O-) and no additional functional groups tend to result in a low yield. The flexibility and decreased rigidity of the catalyst structure negatively impact the reaction. Examples include 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers containing a sulfanyl group (-SH) with a short aliphatic chain (up to 3 carbons) tend to result in a high yield. The sulfanyl group provides strong coordination with the metal center, enhancing catalytic activity. Examples include 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a nitro group (-NO2) on an aromatic ring tend to result in a high yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the nitro group stabilizes the metal center, enhancing the reaction. An example is 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (-CF3) tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the trifluoromethyl group destabilizes the metal center, reducing catalytic activity. An example is 4-[(2,2,2-trifluoroacetyl)amino]butanoic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers containing an indole group tend to result in a high yield. The indole group provides π-π interactions and additional coordination sites, enhancing the stability and reactivity of the catalyst. An example is (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring coordinates with the metal center, enhancing catalytic activity. Examples include pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers containing a formyl group (-CHO) on an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. The formyl group introduces steric hindrance or electronic effects that destabilize the metal center. Examples include 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with an aromatic ring and electron-withdrawing groups such as sulfonyl (-SO2-) or carbonyl (-C=O) groups tend to result in a low yield. These groups may destabilize the metal center. Examples include 4-sulfanylbenzoic acid.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

Traditional Commenter Message:
### Performance Evaluation of Current Rules

1. **Effectiveness of Current Rules:**
   - The current rules appear to be less effective in predicting the loading of modifiers on catalysts accurately. The validation accuracy has decreased from previous iterations (0.76) to 0.542857, indicating a potential issue with the current rule set or model configuration.

2. **Overfitting/Underfitting Assessment:**
   - The significant drop in validation accuracy suggests potential underfitting. The model may not be capturing the underlying patterns in the data effectively, possibly due to overly generalized rules or insufficient complexity in the model.

3. **Discrepancies Analysis:**
   - For molecules where the predicted loading is high but the experimental value is low, rules with high positive SHAP values (e.g., Rule 2, Rule 3, Rule 7) may be contributing to overestimation. Conversely, for molecules where the predicted loading is low but the experimental value is high, rules with high negative SHAP values (e.g., Rule 2, Rule 7, Rule 9) may be contributing to underestimation.

4. **Accuracy Improvements:**
   - The decrease in accuracy metrics suggests that the current rules are not improving the model's performance. This indicates a need for revisiting and refining the rules to better capture the nuances of the data.

5. **Insights from SHAP Analysis:**
   - SHAP analysis highlights specific rules that may be contributing to incorrect predictions. For instance, Rule 2 and Rule 3 often have high positive SHAP values for overestimated loadings, suggesting they may need refinement. Similarly, Rule 7 and Rule 9 have high negative SHAP values for underestimated loadings, indicating potential areas for adjustment.

### Recommendations for Improvement

1. **Refine Overestimated Loading Rules:**
   - **Rule 2 and Rule 3:** Consider revising these rules to account for additional factors that may influence loading, such as steric hindrance or specific electronic effects not currently captured.

2. **Adjust Underestimated Loading Rules:**
   - **Rule 7 and Rule 9:** These rules may need to incorporate additional structural or electronic considerations that could lead to higher loading predictions. For example, exploring the impact of substituents on the aromatic ring or the presence of additional coordination sites.

3. **Improve Generalization:**
   - Introduce more nuanced rules that capture the diversity of molecular structures and their interactions with catalysts. This could involve incorporating machine learning techniques to identify patterns not evident through rule-based approaches alone.

4. **Iterative Refinement:**
   - Use insights from SHAP analysis to iteratively test and refine rules. This could involve creating new rules based on observed patterns in SHAP values or modifying existing rules to better align with experimental data.

5. **Incorporate Additional Features:**
   - Consider expanding the feature matrix to include more detailed molecular descriptors or environmental factors that could influence catalyst loading. This could help improve the model's ability to generalize across different datasets.

By addressing these areas, the model's performance can be improved, leading to more accurate predictions and a better understanding of the factors influencing catalyst loading.

    **Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing a carboxylic acid group (-COOH) and an aromatic ring with electron-donating substituents (e.g., -OH, -NH2) tend to result in a high yield. The electron-donating groups enhance coordination with the metal center, stabilizing the catalyst. Examples include 4-aminobenzoic acid and 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with an amino group (-NH2) and a linear aliphatic chain of 4 to 6 carbons, without additional electron-withdrawing groups, tend to result in a high yield. The amino group enhances coordination, while the aliphatic chain provides steric effects that favor the reaction. Examples include 5-aminopentanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a hydroxyl group (-OH) and an aromatic ring with additional electron-donating groups tend to result in a high yield. The hydroxyl group participates in hydrogen bonding, stabilizing the catalyst structure. Examples include 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple ether linkages (-O-) and no additional functional groups tend to result in a low yield. The flexibility and decreased rigidity of the catalyst structure negatively impact the reaction. Examples include 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers containing a sulfanyl group (-SH) with a short aliphatic chain (up to 3 carbons) tend to result in a high yield. The sulfanyl group provides strong coordination with the metal center, enhancing catalytic activity. Examples include 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a nitro group (-NO2) on an aromatic ring tend to result in a high yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the nitro group stabilizes the metal center, enhancing the reaction. An example is 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (-CF3) tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the trifluoromethyl group destabilizes the metal center, reducing catalytic activity. An example is 4-[(2,2,2-trifluoroacetyl)amino]butanoic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers containing an indole group tend to result in a high yield. The indole group provides π-π interactions and additional coordination sites, enhancing the stability and reactivity of the catalyst. An example is (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring coordinates with the metal center, enhancing catalytic activity. Examples include pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers containing a formyl group (-CHO) on an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. The formyl group introduces steric hindrance or electronic effects that destabilize the metal center. Examples include 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with an aromatic ring and electron-withdrawing groups such as sulfonyl (-SO2-) or carbonyl (-C=O) groups tend to result in a low yield. These groups may destabilize the metal center. Examples include 4-sulfanylbenzoic acid.

Rule Generator Message:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing a carboxylic acid group (-COOH) and an aromatic ring with electron-donating substituents (e.g., -OH, -NH2) tend to result in a high yield. The electron-donating groups enhance coordination with the metal center, stabilizing the catalyst. Examples include 4-aminobenzoic acid and 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with an amino group (-NH2) and a linear aliphatic chain of 4 to 6 carbons, without additional electron-withdrawing groups, tend to result in a high yield. The amino group enhances coordination, while the aliphatic chain provides steric effects that favor the reaction. Examples include 5-aminopentanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a hydroxyl group (-OH) and an aromatic ring with additional electron-donating groups tend to result in a high yield. The hydroxyl group participates in hydrogen bonding, stabilizing the catalyst structure. Examples include 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple ether linkages (-O-) and no additional functional groups tend to result in a low yield. The flexibility and decreased rigidity of the catalyst structure negatively impact the reaction. Examples include 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers containing a sulfanyl group (-SH) with a short aliphatic chain (up to 3 carbons) tend to result in a high yield. The sulfanyl group provides strong coordination with the metal center, enhancing catalytic activity. Examples include 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a nitro group (-NO2) on an aromatic ring tend to result in a high yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the nitro group stabilizes the metal center, enhancing the reaction. An example is 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (-CF3) tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the trifluoromethyl group destabilizes the metal center, reducing catalytic activity. An example is 4-[(2,2,2-trifluoroacetyl)amino]butanoic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers containing an indole group tend to result in a high yield. The indole group provides π-π interactions and additional coordination sites, enhancing the stability and reactivity of the catalyst. An example is (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring coordinates with the metal center, enhancing catalytic activity. Examples include pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers containing a formyl group (-CHO) on an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. The formyl group introduces steric hindrance or electronic effects that destabilize the metal center. Examples include 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with an aromatic ring and electron-withdrawing groups such as sulfonyl (-SO2-) or carbonyl (-C=O) groups tend to result in a low yield. These groups may destabilize the metal center. Examples include 4-sulfanylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with an aromatic ring and electron-donating groups such as methoxy (-OCH3) or ethoxy (-OC2H5) tend to result in a high yield. These groups enhance the electron density on the aromatic ring, stabilizing the metal center. An example is 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a branched aliphatic chain containing an amino group (-NH2) tend to result in a low yield. The branching may introduce steric hindrance that affects coordination with the metal center. An example is (2S)-6-acetamido-2-aminohexanoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers containing a pyridine ring with electron-withdrawing substituents tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature reduces the electron density on the nitrogen, affecting coordination. An example is 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a long aliphatic chain (more than 6 carbons) and no additional functional groups tend to result in a low yield. The long chain may introduce steric hindrance and reduce effective coordination. An example is octanoic acid.

**End of Rules**

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[c][OX2H]', '[c][NX3;H2,H1][c]'],  # Rule 1
        ['[NX3;H2]', '[C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4]'],  # Rule 2
        ['[OX2H]', '[c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 3
        ['[OX2][C;!R][OX2]'],  # Rule 4
        ['[SX2H]', '[C;X4][C;X4][C;X4]'],  # Rule 5
        ['[c][NX3+](=O)[O-]'],  # Rule 6
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 7
        ['[c]1[nH]c2c(c1)cccc2'],  # Rule 8
        ['[n]1ccccc1'],  # Rule 9
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 10
        ['[c][SX4](=O)(=O)[#6]'],  # Rule 11
        ['[c][OX2][C;!R]'],  # Rule 12
        ['[NX3;H2][C;X4][C;X4]'],  # Rule 13
        ['[n]1ccccc1[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 14
        ['[C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4]'],  # Rule 15
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 5, 8, 11]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers containing a formyl group (-CHO) on an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. The formyl group introduces steric hindrance or electronic effects that destabilize the metal center. Examples include 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with an aromatic ring and electron-withdrawing groups such as sulfonyl (-SO2-) or carbonyl (-C=O) groups tend to result in a low yield. These groups may destabilize the metal center. Examples include 4-sulfanylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with an aromatic ring and electron-donating groups such as methoxy (-OCH3) or ethoxy (-OC2H5) tend to result in a high yield. These groups enhance the electron density on the aromatic ring, stabilizing the metal center. An example is 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a branched aliphatic chain containing an amino group (-NH2) tend to result in a low yield. The branching may introduce steric hindrance that affects coordination with the metal center. An example is (2S)-6-acetamido-2-aminohexanoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers containing a pyridine ring with electron-withdrawing substituents tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature reduces the electron density on the nitrogen, affecting coordination. An example is 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a long aliphatic chain (more than 6 carbons) and no additional functional groups tend to result in a low yield. The long chain may introduce steric hindrance and reduce effective coordination. An example is octanoic acid.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[c][OX2H]', '[c][NX3;H2,H1][c]'],  # Rule 1
        ['[NX3;H2]', '[C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4]'],  # Rule 2
        ['[OX2H]', '[c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 3
        ['[OX2][C;!R][OX2]'],  # Rule 4
        ['[SX2H]', '[C;X4][C;X4][C;X4]'],  # Rule 5
        ['[c][NX3+](=O)[O-]'],  # Rule 6
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 7
        ['[c]1[nH]c2c(c1)cccc2'],  # Rule 8
        ['[n]1ccccc1'],  # Rule 9
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 10
        ['[c][SX4](=O)(=O)[#6]'],  # Rule 11
        ['[c][OX2][C;!R]'],  # Rule 12
        ['[NX3;H2][C;X4][C;X4]'],  # Rule 13
        ['[n]1ccccc1[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 14
        ['[C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4]'],  # Rule 15
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 5, 8, 11]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

Current rules:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing a carboxylic acid group (-COOH) and an aromatic ring with electron-donating substituents (e.g., -OH, -NH2) tend to result in a high yield. The electron-donating groups enhance coordination with the metal center, stabilizing the catalyst. Examples include 4-aminobenzoic acid and 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with an amino group (-NH2) and a linear aliphatic chain of 4 to 6 carbons, without additional electron-withdrawing groups, tend to result in a high yield. The amino group enhances coordination, while the aliphatic chain provides steric effects that favor the reaction. Examples include 5-aminopentanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a hydroxyl group (-OH) and an aromatic ring with additional electron-donating groups tend to result in a high yield. The hydroxyl group participates in hydrogen bonding, stabilizing the catalyst structure. Examples include 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple ether linkages (-O-) and no additional functional groups tend to result in a low yield. The flexibility and decreased rigidity of the catalyst structure negatively impact the reaction. Examples include 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers containing a sulfanyl group (-SH) with a short aliphatic chain (up to 3 carbons) tend to result in a high yield. The sulfanyl group provides strong coordination with the metal center, enhancing catalytic activity. Examples include 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a nitro group (-NO2) on an aromatic ring tend to result in a high yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the nitro group stabilizes the metal center, enhancing the reaction. An example is 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (-CF3) tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the trifluoromethyl group destabilizes the metal center, reducing catalytic activity. An example is 4-[(2,2,2-trifluoroacetyl)amino]butanoic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers containing an indole group tend to result in a high yield. The indole group provides π-π interactions and additional coordination sites, enhancing the stability and reactivity of the catalyst. An example is (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring coordinates with the metal center, enhancing catalytic activity. Examples include pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers containing a formyl group (-CHO) on an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. The formyl group introduces steric hindrance or electronic effects that destabilize the metal center. Examples include 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with an aromatic ring and electron-withdrawing groups such as sulfonyl (-SO2-) or carbonyl (-C=O) groups tend to result in a low yield. These groups may destabilize the metal center. Examples include 4-sulfanylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with an aromatic ring and electron-donating groups such as methoxy (-OCH3) or ethoxy (-OC2H5) tend to result in a high yield. These groups enhance the electron density on the aromatic ring, stabilizing the metal center. An example is 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a branched aliphatic chain containing an amino group (-NH2) tend to result in a low yield. The branching may introduce steric hindrance that affects coordination with the metal center. An example is (2S)-6-acetamido-2-aminohexanoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers containing a pyridine ring with electron-withdrawing substituents tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature reduces the electron density on the nitrogen, affecting coordination. An example is 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a long aliphatic chain (more than 6 carbons) and no additional functional groups tend to result in a low yield. The long chain may introduce steric hindrance and reduce effective coordination. An example is octanoic acid.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

Traditional Commenter Message:
### Performance Evaluation of Current Rules

1. **Effectiveness of Current Rules:**
   - The current rules seem to be struggling with effectiveness, as indicated by the declining validation accuracy from 0.76 in previous iterations to 0.514 in the current iteration. This suggests that the rules may not be capturing the underlying patterns in the data effectively.

2. **Overfitting/Underfitting:**
   - The consistent decrease in validation accuracy suggests potential overfitting, where the model might be too tailored to the training data and not generalizing well to new data. The addition of new rules (e.g., Rule 12, Rule 13, Rule 15) might have introduced complexity that the model cannot handle effectively.

3. **Discrepancies Analysis:**
   - For molecules where the predicted loading is high but the experimental value is low, rules with high positive SHAP values (e.g., Rule 13 for C(CCCC(=O)O)CCCN) might be problematic.
   - Conversely, for molecules where the predicted loading is low but the experimental value is high, rules with high negative SHAP values (e.g., Rule 13 for C([C@@H](C(=O)O)N)C(=O)O) might need adjustment.

4. **Accuracy Improvements:**
   - The decline in accuracy metrics suggests that the current rules are not improving the model's performance. The probability of improvement seems low without significant changes to the rules.

5. **Insights from SHAP Analysis:**
   - SHAP analysis indicates that certain rules (e.g., Rule 13 and Rule 15) are contributing to incorrect predictions. These rules might need refinement to better capture the relationship between molecular features and catalyst loading.

### Recommendations for Improvement

1. **Refine Rules with High Positive SHAP Values:**
   - Rules like Rule 13, which have high positive SHAP values for overestimated loadings, should be revisited. Consider whether the conditions in these rules are too broad or if they need additional constraints to prevent overestimation.

2. **Adjust Rules with High Negative SHAP Values:**
   - Rules with high negative SHAP values, such as Rule 13 for underestimated loadings, should be adjusted to better capture the conditions that lead to high experimental values. This might involve relaxing some constraints or adding new conditions that account for overlooked features.

3. **Improve Generalization:**
   - Simplify the rules to reduce complexity and improve generalization. This could involve merging similar rules or removing redundant conditions that do not contribute significantly to the model's performance.

4. **Iterative Refinement:**
   - Use insights from SHAP analysis to iteratively refine the rules. Focus on rules that consistently show high SHAP values (positive or negative) and assess whether they align with the chemical intuition and experimental data.

5. **Evaluate Rule Effectiveness:**

By addressing these areas, the rules can be improved to better capture the relationship between molecular features and catalyst loading, ultimately enhancing the model's predictive performance.

    Current_Rules:
    **Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing a carboxylic acid group (-COOH) and an aromatic ring with electron-donating substituents (e.g., -OH, -NH2) tend to result in a high yield. The electron-donating groups enhance coordination with the metal center, stabilizing the catalyst. Examples include 4-aminobenzoic acid and 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with an amino group (-NH2) and a linear aliphatic chain of 4 to 6 carbons, without additional electron-withdrawing groups, tend to result in a high yield. The amino group enhances coordination, while the aliphatic chain provides steric effects that favor the reaction. Examples include 5-aminopentanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a hydroxyl group (-OH) and an aromatic ring with additional electron-donating groups tend to result in a high yield. The hydroxyl group participates in hydrogen bonding, stabilizing the catalyst structure. Examples include 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple ether linkages (-O-) and no additional functional groups tend to result in a low yield. The flexibility and decreased rigidity of the catalyst structure negatively impact the reaction. Examples include 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers containing a sulfanyl group (-SH) with a short aliphatic chain (up to 3 carbons) tend to result in a high yield. The sulfanyl group provides strong coordination with the metal center, enhancing catalytic activity. Examples include 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a nitro group (-NO2) on an aromatic ring tend to result in a high yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the nitro group stabilizes the metal center, enhancing the reaction. An example is 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (-CF3) tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the trifluoromethyl group destabilizes the metal center, reducing catalytic activity. An example is 4-[(2,2,2-trifluoroacetyl)amino]butanoic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers containing an indole group tend to result in a high yield. The indole group provides π-π interactions and additional coordination sites, enhancing the stability and reactivity of the catalyst. An example is (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring coordinates with the metal center, enhancing catalytic activity. Examples include pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers containing a formyl group (-CHO) on an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. The formyl group introduces steric hindrance or electronic effects that destabilize the metal center. Examples include 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with an aromatic ring and electron-withdrawing groups such as sulfonyl (-SO2-) or carbonyl (-C=O) groups tend to result in a low yield. These groups may destabilize the metal center. Examples include 4-sulfanylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with an aromatic ring and electron-donating groups such as methoxy (-OCH3) or ethoxy (-OC2H5) tend to result in a high yield. These groups enhance the electron density on the aromatic ring, stabilizing the metal center. An example is 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a branched aliphatic chain containing an amino group (-NH2) tend to result in a low yield. The branching may introduce steric hindrance that affects coordination with the metal center. An example is (2S)-6-acetamido-2-aminohexanoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers containing a pyridine ring with electron-withdrawing substituents tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature reduces the electron density on the nitrogen, affecting coordination. An example is 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a long aliphatic chain (more than 6 carbons) and no additional functional groups tend to result in a low yield. The long chain may introduce steric hindrance and reduce effective coordination. An example is octanoic acid.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

- **Comment 13**: Rule 13 is clear and provides insight into the steric effects of branched aliphatic chains. It is simple but effective, focusing on the branching. Supported by examples like (2S)-6-acetamido-2-aminohexanoic acid. Score: 4/5.

- **Comment 14**: Rule 14 is clear and provides insight into the effects of electron-withdrawing substituents on pyridine rings. It is simple but effective, focusing on the substituents. Supported by examples like 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid. Score: 4/5.

- **Comment 15**: Rule 15 is clear and provides insight into the steric effects of long aliphatic chains. It is simple but effective, focusing on the chain length. Supported by examples like octanoic acid. Score: 4/5.

**End of Comments**

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[c][OX2H]', '[c][NX3H2]'],  # Rule 1: Carboxylic acid and aromatic ring with electron-donating groups
        ['[NX3H2]', '[C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4]'],  # Rule 2: Amino group and linear aliphatic chain
        ['[OX2H]', '[c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 3: Hydroxyl group and aromatic ring with electron-donating groups
        ['[OX2][C;X4][OX2]'],  # Rule 4: Multiple ether linkages
        ['[SX2H]', '[C;X4][C;X4][C;X4]'],  # Rule 5: Sulfanyl group with short aliphatic chain
        ['[NX3+](=O)[O-]', '[c]'],  # Rule 6: Nitro group on an aromatic ring
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 7: Trifluoromethyl group
        ['[c]1[nH]c2c(c1)cccc2'],  # Rule 8: Indole group
        ['[n]1ccccc1'],  # Rule 9: Pyridine ring
        ['[CX3H]=O', '[c]'],  # Rule 10: Formyl group on an aromatic ring
        ['[c][SX4](=O)(=O)'],  # Rule 11: Aromatic ring with sulfonyl or carbonyl groups
        ['[c][OX2][C;X4][OX2]'],  # Rule 12: Aromatic ring with methoxy or ethoxy groups
        ['[NX3H2]', '[C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4]'],  # Rule 13: Branched aliphatic chain with amino group
        ['[n]1ccccc1', '[c][SX4](=O)(=O)'],  # Rule 14: Pyridine ring with electron-withdrawing substituents
        ['[C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4]']  # Rule 15: Long aliphatic chain
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 5, 8, 11]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

Current rules:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing a carboxylic acid group (-COOH) and an aromatic ring with electron-donating substituents (e.g., -OH, -NH2) tend to result in a high yield. These groups enhance coordination with the metal center, stabilizing the catalyst. Examples include 4-aminobenzoic acid and 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with an amino group (-NH2) and a linear aliphatic chain of 4 to 6 carbons, without additional electron-withdrawing groups, tend to result in a high yield. The amino group enhances coordination, while the aliphatic chain provides steric effects that favor the reaction. Examples include 5-aminopentanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a hydroxyl group (-OH) and an aromatic ring with additional electron-donating groups tend to result in a high yield. The hydroxyl group participates in hydrogen bonding, stabilizing the catalyst structure. Examples include 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple ether linkages (-O-) and no additional functional groups tend to result in a low yield. The flexibility and decreased rigidity of the catalyst structure negatively impact the reaction. Examples include 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers containing a sulfanyl group (-SH) with a short aliphatic chain (up to 3 carbons) tend to result in a high yield. The sulfanyl group provides strong coordination with the metal center, enhancing catalytic activity. Examples include 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a nitro group (-NO2) on an aromatic ring tend to result in a high yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the nitro group stabilizes the metal center, enhancing the reaction. An example is 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (-CF3) tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the trifluoromethyl group destabilizes the metal center, reducing catalytic activity. An example is 4-[(2,2,2-trifluoroacetyl)amino]butanoic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers containing an indole group tend to result in a high yield. The indole group provides π-π interactions and additional coordination sites, enhancing the stability and reactivity of the catalyst. An example is (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring coordinates with the metal center, enhancing catalytic activity. Examples include pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers containing a formyl group (-CHO) on an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. The formyl group introduces steric hindrance or electronic effects that destabilize the metal center. Examples include 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with an aromatic ring and electron-withdrawing groups such as sulfonyl (-SO2-) or carbonyl (-C=O) groups tend to result in a low yield. These groups may destabilize the metal center. Examples include 4-sulfanylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with an aromatic ring and electron-donating groups such as methoxy (-OCH3) or ethoxy (-OC2H5) tend to result in a high yield. These groups enhance the electron density on the aromatic ring, stabilizing the metal center. An example is 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a branched aliphatic chain containing an amino group (-NH2) tend to result in a low yield. The branching may introduce steric hindrance that affects coordination with the metal center. An example is (2S)-6-acetamido-2-aminohexanoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers containing a pyridine ring with electron-withdrawing substituents tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature reduces the electron density on the nitrogen, affecting coordination. An example is 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a long aliphatic chain (more than 6 carbons) and no additional functional groups tend to result in a low yield. The long chain may introduce steric hindrance and reduce effective coordination. An example is octanoic acid.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[c][OH]', '[c][NH2]'],  # Rule 1: Carboxylic acid and aromatic ring with electron-donating groups
        ['[NX3H2]', '[C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4]'],  # Rule 2: Amino group and linear aliphatic chain
        ['[OX2H]', '[c][OH]', '[c][NH2]'],  # Rule 3: Hydroxyl group and aromatic ring with electron-donating groups
        ['[OX2][C;X4][OX2]', '[OX2][C;X4][OX2]'],  # Rule 4: Multiple ether linkages
        ['[SX2H]', '[C;X4][C;X4][C;X4]'],  # Rule 5: Sulfanyl group with short aliphatic chain
        ['[c][NX3+](=O)[O-]'],  # Rule 6: Nitro group on an aromatic ring
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 7: Trifluoromethyl group
        ['[c]1[nH]c2c(c1)cccc2'],  # Rule 8: Indole group
        ['[n]1ccccc1'],  # Rule 9: Pyridine ring
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 10: Formyl group on an aromatic ring
        ['[c][SX4](=O)(=O)', '[c][CX3](=O)'],  # Rule 11: Aromatic ring with sulfonyl or carbonyl groups
        ['[c][OX2][CH3]', '[c][OX2][CH2][CH3]'],  # Rule 12: Aromatic ring with methoxy or ethoxy groups
        ['[NX3H2]', '[C;X4]([C;X4])[C;X4][C;X4]'],  # Rule 13: Branched aliphatic chain with amino group
        ['[n]1ccccc1', '[c][CX3](=O)'],  # Rule 14: Pyridine ring with electron-withdrawing substituents
        ['[C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4]']  # Rule 15: Long aliphatic chain
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 5, 8, 11]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

Current rules:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing a carboxylic acid group (-COOH) and an aromatic ring with electron-donating substituents (e.g., -OH, -NH2) tend to result in a high yield. These groups enhance coordination with the metal center, stabilizing the catalyst. Examples include 4-aminobenzoic acid and 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with an amino group (-NH2) and a linear aliphatic chain of 4 to 6 carbons, without additional electron-withdrawing groups, tend to result in a high yield. The amino group enhances coordination, while the aliphatic chain provides steric effects that favor the reaction. Examples include 5-aminopentanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a hydroxyl group (-OH) and an aromatic ring with additional electron-donating groups tend to result in a high yield. The hydroxyl group participates in hydrogen bonding, stabilizing the catalyst structure. Examples include 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple ether linkages (-O-) and no additional functional groups tend to result in a low yield. The flexibility and decreased rigidity of the catalyst structure negatively impact the reaction. Examples include 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers containing a sulfanyl group (-SH) with a short aliphatic chain (up to 3 carbons) tend to result in a high yield. The sulfanyl group provides strong coordination with the metal center, enhancing catalytic activity. Examples include 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a nitro group (-NO2) on an aromatic ring tend to result in a high yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the nitro group stabilizes the metal center, enhancing the reaction. An example is 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (-CF3) tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the trifluoromethyl group destabilizes the metal center, reducing catalytic activity. An example is 4-[(2,2,2-trifluoroacetyl)amino]butanoic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers containing an indole group tend to result in a high yield. The indole group provides π-π interactions and additional coordination sites, enhancing the stability and reactivity of the catalyst. An example is (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring coordinates with the metal center, enhancing catalytic activity. Examples include pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers containing a formyl group (-CHO) on an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. The formyl group introduces steric hindrance or electronic effects that destabilize the metal center. Examples include 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with an aromatic ring and electron-withdrawing groups such as sulfonyl (-SO2-) or carbonyl (-C=O) groups tend to result in a low yield. These groups may destabilize the metal center. Examples include 4-sulfanylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with an aromatic ring and electron-donating groups such as methoxy (-OCH3) or ethoxy (-OC2H5) tend to result in a high yield. These groups enhance the electron density on the aromatic ring, stabilizing the metal center. An example is 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a branched aliphatic chain containing an amino group (-NH2) tend to result in a low yield. The branching may introduce steric hindrance that affects coordination with the metal center. An example is (2S)-6-acetamido-2-aminohexanoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers containing a pyridine ring with electron-withdrawing substituents tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature reduces the electron density on the nitrogen, affecting coordination. An example is 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a long aliphatic chain (more than 6 carbons) and no additional functional groups tend to result in a low yield. The long chain may introduce steric hindrance and reduce effective coordination. An example is octanoic acid.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

    **Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing a carboxylic acid group (-COOH) and an aromatic ring with electron-donating substituents (e.g., -OH, -NH2) tend to result in a high yield. These groups enhance coordination with the metal center, stabilizing the catalyst. Examples include 4-aminobenzoic acid and 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with an amino group (-NH2) and a linear aliphatic chain of 4 to 6 carbons, without additional electron-withdrawing groups, tend to result in a high yield. The amino group enhances coordination, while the aliphatic chain provides steric effects that favor the reaction. Examples include 5-aminopentanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a hydroxyl group (-OH) and an aromatic ring with additional electron-donating groups tend to result in a high yield. The hydroxyl group participates in hydrogen bonding, stabilizing the catalyst structure. Examples include 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple ether linkages (-O-) and no additional functional groups tend to result in a low yield. The flexibility and decreased rigidity of the catalyst structure negatively impact the reaction. Examples include 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers containing a sulfanyl group (-SH) with a short aliphatic chain (up to 3 carbons) tend to result in a high yield. The sulfanyl group provides strong coordination with the metal center, enhancing catalytic activity. Examples include 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a nitro group (-NO2) on an aromatic ring tend to result in a high yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the nitro group stabilizes the metal center, enhancing the reaction. An example is 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (-CF3) tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the trifluoromethyl group destabilizes the metal center, reducing catalytic activity. An example is 4-[(2,2,2-trifluoroacetyl)amino]butanoic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers containing an indole group tend to result in a high yield. The indole group provides π-π interactions and additional coordination sites, enhancing the stability and reactivity of the catalyst. An example is (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring coordinates with the metal center, enhancing catalytic activity. Examples include pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers containing a formyl group (-CHO) on an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. The formyl group introduces steric hindrance or electronic effects that destabilize the metal center. Examples include 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with an aromatic ring and electron-withdrawing groups such as sulfonyl (-SO2-) or carbonyl (-C=O) groups tend to result in a low yield. These groups may destabilize the metal center. Examples include 4-sulfanylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with an aromatic ring and electron-donating groups such as methoxy (-OCH3) or ethoxy (-OC2H5) tend to result in a high yield. These groups enhance the electron density on the aromatic ring, stabilizing the metal center. An example is 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a branched aliphatic chain containing an amino group (-NH2) tend to result in a low yield. The branching may introduce steric hindrance that affects coordination with the metal center. An example is (2S)-6-acetamido-2-aminohexanoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers containing a pyridine ring with electron-withdrawing substituents tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature reduces the electron density on the nitrogen, affecting coordination. An example is 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a long aliphatic chain (more than 6 carbons) and no additional functional groups tend to result in a low yield. The long chain may introduce steric hindrance and reduce effective coordination. An example is octanoic acid.

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[c][OX2H]', '[c][NX3H2]'],  # Rule 1
        ['[NX3H2]', '[C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4]'],  # Rule 2
        ['[OX2H]', '[c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 3
        ['[OX2][C;X4][OX2]'],  # Rule 4
        ['[SX2H]', '[C;X4][C;X4][C;X4]'],  # Rule 5
        ['[c][NX3+](=O)[O-]'],  # Rule 6
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 7
        ['c1c[nH]c2c1cccc2'],  # Rule 8
        ['c1ccncc1'],  # Rule 9
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 10
        ['[c][SX4](=O)(=O)'],  # Rule 11
        ['[c][OX2][C;X4][OX2]'],  # Rule 12
        ['[NX3H2][C;X4][C;X4]'],  # Rule 13
        ['c1ccncc1[CX3](=O)'],  # Rule 14
        ['[C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4]'],  # Rule 15
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 5, 8, 11]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

Current rules:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing a carboxylic acid group (-COOH) and an aromatic ring with electron-donating substituents (e.g., -OH, -NH2) tend to result in a high yield. These groups enhance coordination with the metal center, stabilizing the catalyst. Examples include 4-aminobenzoic acid and 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with an amino group (-NH2) and a linear aliphatic chain of 4 to 6 carbons, without additional electron-withdrawing groups, tend to result in a high yield. The amino group enhances coordination, while the aliphatic chain provides steric effects that favor the reaction. Examples include 5-aminopentanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a hydroxyl group (-OH) and an aromatic ring with additional electron-donating groups tend to result in a high yield. The hydroxyl group participates in hydrogen bonding, stabilizing the catalyst structure. Examples include 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple ether linkages (-O-) and no additional functional groups tend to result in a low yield. The flexibility and decreased rigidity of the catalyst structure negatively impact the reaction. Examples include 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers containing a sulfanyl group (-SH) with a short aliphatic chain (up to 3 carbons) tend to result in a high yield. The sulfanyl group provides strong coordination with the metal center, enhancing catalytic activity. Examples include 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a nitro group (-NO2) on an aromatic ring tend to result in a high yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the nitro group stabilizes the metal center, enhancing the reaction. An example is 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (-CF3) tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the trifluoromethyl group destabilizes the metal center, reducing catalytic activity. An example is 4-[(2,2,2-trifluoroacetyl)amino]butanoic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers containing an indole group tend to result in a high yield. The indole group provides π-π interactions and additional coordination sites, enhancing the stability and reactivity of the catalyst. An example is (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring coordinates with the metal center, enhancing catalytic activity. Examples include pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers containing a formyl group (-CHO) on an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. The formyl group introduces steric hindrance or electronic effects that destabilize the metal center. Examples include 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with an aromatic ring and electron-withdrawing groups such as sulfonyl (-SO2-) or carbonyl (-C=O) groups tend to result in a low yield. These groups may destabilize the metal center. Examples include 4-sulfanylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with an aromatic ring and electron-donating groups such as methoxy (-OCH3) or ethoxy (-OC2H5) tend to result in a high yield. These groups enhance the electron density on the aromatic ring, stabilizing the metal center. An example is 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a branched aliphatic chain containing an amino group (-NH2) tend to result in a low yield. The branching may introduce steric hindrance that affects coordination with the metal center. An example is (2S)-6-acetamido-2-aminohexanoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers containing a pyridine ring with electron-withdrawing substituents tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature reduces the electron density on the nitrogen, affecting coordination. An example is 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a long aliphatic chain (more than 6 carbons) and no additional functional groups tend to result in a low yield. The long chain may introduce steric hindrance and reduce effective coordination. An example is octanoic acid.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[c][OX2H]', '[c][NX3H2]'],  # Rule 1
        ['[NX3H2]', '[C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4]'],  # Rule 2
        ['[OX2H]', '[c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 3
        ['[OX2][C;X4][OX2]'],  # Rule 4
        ['[SX2H]', '[C;X4][C;X4][C;X4]'],  # Rule 5
        ['[c][NX3+](=O)[O-]'],  # Rule 6
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 7
        ['c1c[nH]c2c1cccc2'],  # Rule 8
        ['c1ccncc1'],  # Rule 9
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 10
        ['[c][SX4](=O)(=O)'],  # Rule 11
        ['[c][OX2][C;X4][OX2]'],  # Rule 12
        ['[NX3H2][C;X4][C;X4]'],  # Rule 13
        ['c1ccncc1[CX3](=O)'],  # Rule 14
        ['[C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4]'],  # Rule 15
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 5, 8, 11]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df
