- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a hydroxyl group (-OH) and an aromatic ring with additional electron-donating groups tend to result in a high yield. The hydroxyl group participates in hydrogen bonding, stabilizing the catalyst structure. Examples include 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple ether linkages (-O-) and no additional functional groups tend to result in a low yield. The flexibility and decreased rigidity of the catalyst structure negatively impact the reaction. Examples include 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers containing a sulfanyl group (-SH) with a short aliphatic chain (up to 3 carbons) tend to result in a high yield. The sulfanyl group provides strong coordination with the metal center, enhancing catalytic activity. Examples include 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a nitro group (-NO2) on an aromatic ring tend to result in a high yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the nitro group stabilizes the metal center, enhancing the reaction. An example is 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (-CF3) tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the trifluoromethyl group destabilizes the metal center, reducing catalytic activity. An example is 4-[(2,2,2-trifluoroacetyl)amino]butanoic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers containing an indole group tend to result in a high yield. The indole group provides π-π interactions and additional coordination sites, enhancing the stability and reactivity of the catalyst. An example is (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring coordinates with the metal center, enhancing catalytic activity. Examples include pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers containing a formyl group (-CHO) on an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. The formyl group introduces steric hindrance or electronic effects that destabilize the metal center. Examples include 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with an aromatic ring and electron-withdrawing groups such as sulfonyl (-SO2-) or carbonyl (-C=O) groups tend to result in a low yield. These groups may destabilize the metal center. Examples include 4-sulfanylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with an aromatic ring and electron-donating groups such as methoxy (-OCH3) or ethoxy (-OC2H5) tend to result in a high yield. These groups enhance the electron density on the aromatic ring, stabilizing the metal center. An example is 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a branched aliphatic chain containing an amino group (-NH2) tend to result in a low yield. The branching may introduce steric hindrance that affects coordination with the metal center. An example is (2S)-6-acetamido-2-aminohexanoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers containing a pyridine ring with electron-withdrawing substituents tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature reduces the electron density on the nitrogen, affecting coordination. An example is 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a long aliphatic chain (more than 6 carbons) and no additional functional groups tend to result in a low yield. The long chain may introduce steric hindrance and reduce effective coordination. An example is octanoic acid.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

   - **Rule 8**: Re-evaluate the impact of indole groups. While they provide π-π interactions, the overall coordination environment should be considered to ensure accurate predictions.

    **Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing a carboxylic acid group (-COOH) and an aromatic ring with electron-donating substituents (e.g., -OH, -NH2) tend to result in a high yield. These groups enhance coordination with the metal center, stabilizing the catalyst. Examples include 4-aminobenzoic acid and 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with an amino group (-NH2) and a linear aliphatic chain of 4 to 6 carbons, without additional electron-withdrawing groups, tend to result in a high yield. The amino group enhances coordination, while the aliphatic chain provides steric effects that favor the reaction. Examples include 5-aminopentanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a hydroxyl group (-OH) and an aromatic ring with additional electron-donating groups tend to result in a high yield. The hydroxyl group participates in hydrogen bonding, stabilizing the catalyst structure. Examples include 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple ether linkages (-O-) and no additional functional groups tend to result in a low yield. The flexibility and decreased rigidity of the catalyst structure negatively impact the reaction. Examples include 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers containing a sulfanyl group (-SH) with a short aliphatic chain (up to 3 carbons) tend to result in a high yield. The sulfanyl group provides strong coordination with the metal center, enhancing catalytic activity. Examples include 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a nitro group (-NO2) on an aromatic ring tend to result in a high yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the nitro group stabilizes the metal center, enhancing the reaction. An example is 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (-CF3) tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the trifluoromethyl group destabilizes the metal center, reducing catalytic activity. An example is 4-[(2,2,2-trifluoroacetyl)amino]butanoic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers containing an indole group tend to result in a high yield. The indole group provides π-π interactions and additional coordination sites, enhancing the stability and reactivity of the catalyst. An example is (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring coordinates with the metal center, enhancing catalytic activity. Examples include pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers containing a formyl group (-CHO) on an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. The formyl group introduces steric hindrance or electronic effects that destabilize the metal center. Examples include 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with an aromatic ring and electron-withdrawing groups such as sulfonyl (-SO2-) or carbonyl (-C=O) groups tend to result in a low yield. These groups may destabilize the metal center. Examples include 4-sulfanylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with an aromatic ring and electron-donating groups such as methoxy (-OCH3) or ethoxy (-OC2H5) tend to result in a high yield. These groups enhance the electron density on the aromatic ring, stabilizing the metal center. An example is 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a branched aliphatic chain containing an amino group (-NH2) tend to result in a low yield. The branching may introduce steric hindrance that affects coordination with the metal center. An example is (2S)-6-acetamido-2-aminohexanoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers containing a pyridine ring with electron-withdrawing substituents tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature reduces the electron density on the nitrogen, affecting coordination. An example is 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a long aliphatic chain (more than 6 carbons) and no additional functional groups tend to result in a low yield. The long chain may introduce steric hindrance and reduce effective coordination. An example is octanoic acid.

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[c][OX2H]', '[c][NX3H2]'],  # Rule 1
        ['[NX3H2]', '[C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4]'],  # Rule 2
        ['[OX2H]', '[c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 3
        ['[OX2][C;X4][OX2]'],  # Rule 4
        ['[SX2H]', '[C;X4][C;X4][C;X4]'],  # Rule 5
        ['[c][NX3+](=O)[O-]'],  # Rule 6
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 7
        ['c1c[nH]c2c1cccc2'],  # Rule 8
        ['c1ccncc1'],  # Rule 9
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 10
        ['[c][SX4](=O)(=O)'],  # Rule 11
        ['[c][OX2][C;X4][OX2]'],  # Rule 12
        ['[NX3H2]', '[C;X4][C;X4][C;X4]'],  # Rule 13
        ['c1ccncc1', '[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 14
        ['[C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4]']  # Rule 15
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 5, 8, 11]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[c][OX2H]', '[c][NX3H2]'],  # Rule 1
        ['[NX3H2]', '[C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4]'],  # Rule 2
        ['[OX2H]', '[c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 3
        ['[OX2][C;X4][OX2]'],  # Rule 4
        ['[SX2H]', '[C;X4][C;X4][C;X4]'],  # Rule 5
        ['[c][NX3+](=O)[O-]'],  # Rule 6
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 7
        ['c1c[nH]c2c1cccc2'],  # Rule 8
        ['c1ccncc1'],  # Rule 9
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 10
        ['[c][SX4](=O)(=O)'],  # Rule 11
        ['[c][OX2][C;X4][OX2]'],  # Rule 12
        ['[NX3H2]', '[C;X4][C;X4][C;X4]'],  # Rule 13
        ['c1ccncc1', '[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 14
        ['[C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4]']  # Rule 15
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 5, 8, 11]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df
---------------------------------------------------------------
Current rules:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing a carboxylic acid group (-COOH) and an aromatic ring with electron-donating substituents (e.g., -OH, -NH2) tend to result in a high yield. These groups enhance coordination with the metal center, stabilizing the catalyst. Examples include 4-aminobenzoic acid and 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with an amino group (-NH2) and a linear aliphatic chain of 4 to 6 carbons, without additional electron-withdrawing groups, tend to result in a high yield. The amino group enhances coordination, while the aliphatic chain provides steric effects that favor the reaction. Examples include 5-aminopentanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a hydroxyl group (-OH) and an aromatic ring with additional electron-donating groups tend to result in a high yield. The hydroxyl group participates in hydrogen bonding, stabilizing the catalyst structure. Examples include 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple ether linkages (-O-) and no additional functional groups tend to result in a low yield. The flexibility and decreased rigidity of the catalyst structure negatively impact the reaction. Examples include 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers containing a sulfanyl group (-SH) with a short aliphatic chain (up to 3 carbons) tend to result in a high yield. The sulfanyl group provides strong coordination with the metal center, enhancing catalytic activity. Examples include 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a nitro group (-NO2) on an aromatic ring tend to result in a high yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the nitro group stabilizes the metal center, enhancing the reaction. An example is 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (-CF3) tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the trifluoromethyl group destabilizes the metal center, reducing catalytic activity. An example is 4-[(2,2,2-trifluoroacetyl)amino]butanoic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers containing an indole group tend to result in a high yield. The indole group provides π-π interactions and additional coordination sites, enhancing the stability and reactivity of the catalyst. An example is (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring coordinates with the metal center, enhancing catalytic activity. Examples include pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers containing a formyl group (-CHO) on an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. The formyl group introduces steric hindrance or electronic effects that destabilize the metal center. Examples include 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with an aromatic ring and electron-withdrawing groups such as sulfonyl (-SO2-) or carbonyl (-C=O) groups tend to result in a low yield. These groups may destabilize the metal center. Examples include 4-sulfanylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with an aromatic ring and electron-donating groups such as methoxy (-OCH3) or ethoxy (-OC2H5) tend to result in a high yield. These groups enhance the electron density on the aromatic ring, stabilizing the metal center. An example is 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a branched aliphatic chain containing an amino group (-NH2) tend to result in a low yield. The branching may introduce steric hindrance that affects coordination with the metal center. An example is (2S)-6-acetamido-2-aminohexanoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers containing a pyridine ring with electron-withdrawing substituents tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature reduces the electron density on the nitrogen, affecting coordination. An example is 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a long aliphatic chain (more than 6 carbons) and no additional functional groups tend to result in a low yield. The long chain may introduce steric hindrance and reduce effective coordination. An example is octanoic acid.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

Traditional Commenter Message:
### Performance Evaluation of Current Rules

1. **Effectiveness of Current Rules:**
   - The current rules have shown some effectiveness, as indicated by the validation accuracy of 0.6857, which is an improvement from some of the previous iterations where accuracy was as low as 0.5143. However, the accuracy is still not consistently high across all iterations, suggesting that the rules may not be fully capturing the complexity of the data.

2. **Overfitting/Underfitting Assessment:**
   - The fluctuation in validation accuracy across different iterations suggests potential issues with overfitting or underfitting. The rules might be too specific to certain patterns in the training data, leading to overfitting, or they might be too general, failing to capture important nuances, leading to underfitting.

3. **Discrepancies Analysis:**
   - For molecules where the predicted loading is high but the experimental value is low, rules with high positive SHAP values (e.g., Rule 7, Rule 10, Rule 13) might be contributing to overestimation. Conversely, for molecules where the predicted loading is low but the experimental value is high, rules with high negative SHAP values (e.g., Rule 13, Rule 15) might be contributing to underestimation.

4. **Accuracy Improvements:**
   - The improvement in accuracy from earlier iterations suggests that the rules are moving in the right direction, but there is still room for refinement. The current accuracy indicates that the rules are capturing some relevant features but may need further tuning to improve predictive performance.

5. **Insights from SHAP Analysis:**
   - SHAP analysis highlights specific rules that consistently contribute to incorrect predictions. For instance, Rule 13 often has a high positive SHAP value for overestimated loadings, indicating it might be too lenient or broad. Similarly, Rule 15 often has a high negative SHAP value for underestimated loadings, suggesting it might be too restrictive.

### Recommendations for Improvement

1. **Refine Overestimated Loading Rules:**
   - **Rule 7 (Trifluoromethyl group):** Consider revising the conditions under which this rule applies, as it might be overestimating the impact of trifluoromethyl groups on loading.
   - **Rule 10 (Formyl group):** Re-evaluate the impact of formyl groups on aromatic rings, as this rule might be contributing to overestimation in certain contexts.

2. **Adjust Underestimated Loading Rules:**
   - **Rule 13 (Branched aliphatic chain):** This rule might be too restrictive. Consider allowing for exceptions where branching does not significantly hinder coordination.
   - **Rule 15 (Long aliphatic chain):** Reassess the impact of chain length, as this rule might be underestimating the potential for effective coordination in some cases.

3. **Improve Generalization:**
   - Introduce more nuanced rules that consider the interplay between different functional groups and their collective impact on loading. This could help address both overfitting and underfitting by capturing more complex patterns.

4. **Iterative Refinement:**
   - Use insights from SHAP analysis to iteratively test and refine rules. For example, if a rule consistently shows high SHAP values for incorrect predictions, experiment with modifying or splitting the rule to better capture the underlying chemistry.

5. **Incorporate Additional Features:**
   - Consider incorporating additional features or modifying existing ones to capture more subtle effects, such as steric hindrance or electronic interactions, which might not be fully accounted for in the current rules.

By addressing these areas, the rules can be refined to improve both the accuracy and generalization of the model, leading to more reliable predictions of modifier loading on catalysts.

Final Metric Message:

    Target Name: yield
    GPT Model: gpt-4o-2024-08-06
    ML Model: ETC
    Current_Rules:
    **Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing a carboxylic acid group (-COOH) and an aromatic ring with electron-donating substituents (e.g., -OH, -NH2) tend to result in a high yield. These groups enhance coordination with the metal center, stabilizing the catalyst. Examples include 4-aminobenzoic acid and 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with an amino group (-NH2) and a linear aliphatic chain of 4 to 6 carbons, without additional electron-withdrawing groups, tend to result in a high yield. The amino group enhances coordination, while the aliphatic chain provides steric effects that favor the reaction. Examples include 5-aminopentanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a hydroxyl group (-OH) and an aromatic ring with additional electron-donating groups tend to result in a high yield. The hydroxyl group participates in hydrogen bonding, stabilizing the catalyst structure. Examples include 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple ether linkages (-O-) and no additional functional groups tend to result in a low yield. The flexibility and decreased rigidity of the catalyst structure negatively impact the reaction. Examples include 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers containing a sulfanyl group (-SH) with a short aliphatic chain (up to 3 carbons) tend to result in a high yield. The sulfanyl group provides strong coordination with the metal center, enhancing catalytic activity. Examples include 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a nitro group (-NO2) on an aromatic ring tend to result in a high yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the nitro group stabilizes the metal center, enhancing the reaction. An example is 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (-CF3) tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the trifluoromethyl group destabilizes the metal center, reducing catalytic activity. An example is 4-[(2,2,2-trifluoroacetyl)amino]butanoic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers containing an indole group tend to result in a high yield. The indole group provides π-π interactions and additional coordination sites, enhancing the stability and reactivity of the catalyst. An example is (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring coordinates with the metal center, enhancing catalytic activity. Examples include pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers containing a formyl group (-CHO) on an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. The formyl group introduces steric hindrance or electronic effects that destabilize the metal center. Examples include 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with an aromatic ring and electron-withdrawing groups such as sulfonyl (-SO2-) or carbonyl (-C=O) groups tend to result in a low yield. These groups may destabilize the metal center. Examples include 4-sulfanylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with an aromatic ring and electron-donating groups such as methoxy (-OCH3) or ethoxy (-OC2H5) tend to result in a high yield. These groups enhance the electron density on the aromatic ring, stabilizing the metal center. An example is 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a branched aliphatic chain containing an amino group (-NH2) tend to result in a low yield. The branching may introduce steric hindrance that affects coordination with the metal center. An example is (2S)-6-acetamido-2-aminohexanoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers containing a pyridine ring with electron-withdrawing substituents tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature reduces the electron density on the nitrogen, affecting coordination. An example is 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a long aliphatic chain (more than 6 carbons) and no additional functional groups tend to result in a low yield. The long chain may introduce steric hindrance and reduce effective coordination. An example is octanoic acid.

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing a carboxylic acid group (-COOH) and an aromatic ring with electron-donating substituents (e.g., -OH, -NH2) tend to result in a high yield. - **Rule 2**: Modifiers with an amino group (-NH2) and a linear aliphatic chain of 4 to 6 carbons, without additional electron-withdrawing groups, tend to result in a high yield. The amino group enhances coordination, while the aliphatic chain provides steric effects that favor the reaction. Examples include 5-aminopentanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a hydroxyl group (-OH) and an aromatic ring with additional electron-donating groups tend to result in a high yield. The hydroxyl group participates in hydrogen bonding, stabilizing the catalyst structure. Examples include 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple ether linkages (-O-) and no additional functional groups tend to result in a low yield. The flexibility and decreased rigidity of the catalyst structure negatively impact the reaction. Examples include 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers containing a sulfanyl group (-SH) with a short aliphatic chain (up to 3 carbons) tend to result in a high yield. The sulfanyl group provides strong coordination with the metal center, enhancing catalytic activity. Examples include 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a nitro group (-NO2) on an aromatic ring tend to result in a high yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the nitro group stabilizes the metal center, enhancing the reaction. An example is 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (-CF3) and additional electron-donating groups on the aromatic ring can result in a high yield. The electron-donating groups may counteract the destabilizing effect of the trifluoromethyl group. An example is 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers containing an indole group tend to result in a high yield. The indole group provides π-π interactions and additional coordination sites, enhancing the stability and reactivity of the catalyst. An example is (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring coordinates with the metal center, enhancing catalytic activity. Examples include pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers containing a formyl group (-CHO) on an aromatic ring with additional electron-donating groups may result in a high yield. The electron-donating groups can mitigate the negative impact of the formyl group. An example is 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with an aromatic ring and electron-withdrawing groups such as sulfonyl (-SO2-) or carbonyl (-C=O) groups tend to result in a low yield. These groups may destabilize the metal center. Examples include 4-sulfanylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a branched aliphatic chain containing an amino group (-NH2) and additional electron-donating groups may result in a high yield. The electron-donating groups can enhance coordination despite the branching. An example is (2S)-2-amino-3-phenylpropanoic acid.

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[c][OX2H]', '[c][NX3H2]'],  # Rule 1
        ['[NX3H2]', '[C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4]'],  # Rule 2
        ['[OX2H]', '[c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 3
        ['[OX2][C;X4][OX2]'],  # Rule 4
        ['[SX2H]', '[C;X4][C;X4][C;X4]'],  # Rule 5
        ['[c][NX3+](=O)[O-]'],  # Rule 6
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F', '[c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 7
        ['c1c[nH]c2c1cccc2'],  # Rule 8
        ['c1ccncc1'],  # Rule 9
        ['[CX3H]=O', '[c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 10
        ['[c][SX4](=O)(=O)'],  # Rule 11
        ['[NX3H2]', '[C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4]'],  # Rule 12
        ['[C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4]', '[OX2H]'],  # Rule 13
        ['c1ccncc1', '[c][SX4](=O)(=O)'],  # Rule 14
        ['[c][OX2H]', '[c][OX2H]']  # Rule 15
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 5, 6, 7, 8, 9, 12, 13, 14]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

- ** Suggestion 15 **: For Rule 15, the SMARTS `['[c][OX2H]', '[c][OX2H]']` should be refined to ensure the presence of an aromatic ring with electron-donating groups such as methoxy or ethoxy. The current pattern may not enforce both features.

** End of Suggestions **

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[c][OX2H]', '[c][NX3H2]'],  # Rule 1
        ['[NX3H2]', '[C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4]'],  # Rule 2
        ['[OX2H]', '[c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 3
        ['[OX2][C;X4][OX2]'],  # Rule 4
        ['[SX2H]', '[C;X4][C;X4][C;X4]'],  # Rule 5
        ['[c][NX3+](=O)[O-]'],  # Rule 6
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F', '[c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 7
        ['c1c[nH]c2c1cccc2'],  # Rule 8
        ['c1ccncc1'],  # Rule 9
        ['[CX3H]=O', '[c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 10
        ['[c][SX4](=O)(=O)'],  # Rule 11
        ['[NX3H2]', '[C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4]'],  # Rule 12
        ['[C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4]', '[OX2H]'],  # Rule 13
        ['c1ccncc1', '[c][SX4](=O)(=O)'],  # Rule 14
        ['[c][OX2H]', '[c][OX2H]']  # Rule 15
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 5, 6, 7, 8, 9, 12, 13, 14]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df
---------------------------------------------------------------
Current rules:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing a carboxylic acid group (-COOH) and an aromatic ring with electron-donating substituents (e.g., -OH, -NH2) tend to result in a high yield. These groups enhance coordination with the metal center, stabilizing the catalyst. Examples include 4-aminobenzoic acid and 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with an amino group (-NH2) and a linear aliphatic chain of 4 to 6 carbons, without additional electron-withdrawing groups, tend to result in a high yield. The amino group enhances coordination, while the aliphatic chain provides steric effects that favor the reaction. Examples include 5-aminopentanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a hydroxyl group (-OH) and an aromatic ring with additional electron-donating groups tend to result in a high yield. The hydroxyl group participates in hydrogen bonding, stabilizing the catalyst structure. Examples include 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple ether linkages (-O-) and no additional functional groups tend to result in a low yield. The flexibility and decreased rigidity of the catalyst structure negatively impact the reaction. Examples include 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers containing a sulfanyl group (-SH) with a short aliphatic chain (up to 3 carbons) tend to result in a high yield. The sulfanyl group provides strong coordination with the metal center, enhancing catalytic activity. Examples include 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a nitro group (-NO2) on an aromatic ring tend to result in a high yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the nitro group stabilizes the metal center, enhancing the reaction. An example is 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (-CF3) and additional electron-donating groups on the aromatic ring can result in a high yield. The electron-donating groups may counteract the destabilizing effect of the trifluoromethyl group. An example is 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers containing an indole group tend to result in a high yield. The indole group provides π-π interactions and additional coordination sites, enhancing the stability and reactivity of the catalyst. An example is (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring coordinates with the metal center, enhancing catalytic activity. Examples include pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers containing a formyl group (-CHO) on an aromatic ring with additional electron-donating groups may result in a high yield. The electron-donating groups can mitigate the negative impact of the formyl group. An example is 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with an aromatic ring and electron-withdrawing groups such as sulfonyl (-SO2-) or carbonyl (-C=O) groups tend to result in a low yield. These groups may destabilize the metal center. Examples include 4-sulfanylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a branched aliphatic chain containing an amino group (-NH2) and additional electron-donating groups may result in a high yield. The electron-donating groups can enhance coordination despite the branching. An example is (2S)-2-amino-3-phenylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a long aliphatic chain (more than 6 carbons) and additional electron-donating groups can result in a high yield. The electron-donating groups may enhance coordination and reduce steric hindrance. An example is 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers containing a pyridine ring with electron-withdrawing substituents tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature reduces the electron density on the nitrogen, affecting coordination. An example is 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with an aromatic ring and electron-donating groups such as methoxy (-OCH3) or ethoxy (-OC2H5) tend to result in a high yield. These groups enhance the electron density on the aromatic ring, stabilizing the metal center. An example is 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

    **Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing a carboxylic acid group (-COOH) and an aromatic ring with electron-donating substituents (e.g., -OH, -NH2) tend to result in a high yield. These groups enhance coordination with the metal center, stabilizing the catalyst. Examples include 4-aminobenzoic acid and 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with an amino group (-NH2) and a linear aliphatic chain of 4 to 6 carbons, without additional electron-withdrawing groups, tend to result in a high yield. The amino group enhances coordination, while the aliphatic chain provides steric effects that favor the reaction. Examples include 5-aminopentanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a hydroxyl group (-OH) and an aromatic ring with additional electron-donating groups tend to result in a high yield. The hydroxyl group participates in hydrogen bonding, stabilizing the catalyst structure. Examples include 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple ether linkages (-O-) and no additional functional groups tend to result in a low yield. The flexibility and decreased rigidity of the catalyst structure negatively impact the reaction. Examples include 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers containing a sulfanyl group (-SH) with a short aliphatic chain (up to 3 carbons) tend to result in a high yield. The sulfanyl group provides strong coordination with the metal center, enhancing catalytic activity. Examples include 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a nitro group (-NO2) on an aromatic ring tend to result in a high yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the nitro group stabilizes the metal center, enhancing the reaction. An example is 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (-CF3) and additional electron-donating groups on the aromatic ring can result in a high yield. The electron-donating groups may counteract the destabilizing effect of the trifluoromethyl group. An example is 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers containing an indole group tend to result in a high yield. The indole group provides π-π interactions and additional coordination sites, enhancing the stability and reactivity of the catalyst. An example is (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring coordinates with the metal center, enhancing catalytic activity. Examples include pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers containing a formyl group (-CHO) on an aromatic ring with additional electron-donating groups may result in a high yield. The electron-donating groups can mitigate the negative impact of the formyl group. An example is 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with an aromatic ring and electron-withdrawing groups such as sulfonyl (-SO2-) or carbonyl (-C=O) groups tend to result in a low yield. These groups may destabilize the metal center. Examples include 4-sulfanylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a branched aliphatic chain containing an amino group (-NH2) and additional electron-donating groups may result in a high yield. The electron-donating groups can enhance coordination despite the branching. An example is (2S)-2-amino-3-phenylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a long aliphatic chain (more than 6 carbons) and additional electron-donating groups can result in a high yield. The electron-donating groups may enhance coordination and reduce steric hindrance. An example is 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers containing a pyridine ring with electron-withdrawing substituents tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature reduces the electron density on the nitrogen, affecting coordination. An example is 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with an aromatic ring and electron-donating groups such as methoxy (-OCH3) or ethoxy (-OC2H5) tend to result in a high yield. These groups enhance the electron density on the aromatic ring, stabilizing the metal center. An example is 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[c][OX2H]', '[c][NX3H2]'],  # Rule 1: Carboxylic acid and aromatic ring with electron-donating groups
        ['[NX3H2]', '[C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4]'],  # Rule 2: Amino group and linear aliphatic chain
        ['[OX2H]', '[c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 3: Hydroxyl group and aromatic ring with electron-donating groups
        ['[OX2][C;X4][OX2]'],  # Rule 4: Multiple ether linkages
        ['[SX2H]', '[C;X4][C;X4][C;X4]'],  # Rule 5: Sulfanyl group with short aliphatic chain
        ['[NX3+](=O)[O-]', '[c]'],  # Rule 6: Nitro group on an aromatic ring
        ['c1c[nH]c2c1cccc2'],  # Rule 7: Indole group
        ['c1ccncc1'],  # Rule 8: Pyridine ring
        ['[c][SX4](=O)(=O)', '[c][CX3](=O)'],  # Rule 9: Aromatic ring with sulfonyl or carbonyl groups
        ['[C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4]'],  # Rule 10: Long aliphatic chain
        ['c1ccncc1', '[c][CX3](=O)'],  # Rule 11: Pyridine ring with electron-withdrawing groups
        ['[c][OX2][C;X4][OX2]'],  # Rule 12: Aromatic ring with methoxy or ethoxy groups
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 13: Formyl group on an aromatic ring
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 4, 5, 6, 7, 12]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Rules with low prediction
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

** Start of Suggestions **

- ** Suggestion 1 **: For Rule 1, the SMARTS pattern `['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[c][OX2H]', '[c][NX3H2]']` does not fully capture the requirement of having both a carboxylic acid group and an aromatic ring with electron-donating substituents. The pattern should be adjusted to ensure both conditions are met simultaneously, possibly by using a single SMARTS pattern that combines these features.

- ** Suggestion 2 **: Rule 2's SMARTS pattern `['[NX3H2]', '[C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4]']` should be refined to ensure the amino group is directly connected to a linear aliphatic chain of 4 to 6 carbons. The current pattern may not enforce the linearity or the specific chain length.

- ** Suggestion 3 **: For Rule 3, the SMARTS pattern `['[OX2H]', '[c][OX2H]']` should be modified to ensure the hydroxyl group is part of an aromatic ring with additional electron-donating groups. The current pattern may not enforce the presence of additional electron-donating groups.

- ** Suggestion 4 **: Rule 4's pattern `['[OX2][C;X4][OX2]']` should be checked to ensure it captures multiple ether linkages correctly. The current pattern might not account for the absence of additional functional groups, which is crucial for predicting low yield.

- ** Suggestion 5 **: For Rule 5, the pattern `['[SX2H]', '[C;X4][C;X4][C;X4]']` should be refined to ensure the sulfanyl group is connected to a short aliphatic chain (up to 3 carbons). The current pattern might not enforce the chain length correctly.

- ** Suggestion 6 **: Rule 6's pattern `['[NX3+](=O)[O-]', '[c]']` should be checked to ensure it captures the nitro group on an aromatic ring accurately. The current pattern might not enforce the aromatic context properly.

- ** Suggestion 7 **: For Rule 7, the pattern `['c1c[nH]c2c1cccc2']` seems appropriate for identifying indole groups. However, ensure that the pattern is specific enough to avoid false positives.

- ** Suggestion 8 **: Rule 8's pattern `['c1ccncc1']` for pyridine rings should be checked for specificity, ensuring it does not match other similar structures incorrectly.

- ** Suggestion 9 **: For Rule 9, the pattern `['[c][SX4](=O)(=O)', '[c][CX3](=O)']` should be refined to ensure it captures the presence of sulfonyl or carbonyl groups on an aromatic ring accurately. The current pattern might not enforce the aromatic context properly.

- ** Suggestion 10 **: Rule 10's pattern `['[C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4]']` should be checked to ensure it captures long aliphatic chains correctly. The current pattern might not enforce the absence of additional functional groups.

- ** Suggestion 11 **: For Rule 11, the pattern `['c1ccncc1', '[c][CX3](=O)']` should be refined to ensure it captures pyridine rings with electron-withdrawing groups accurately. The current pattern might not enforce the presence of electron-withdrawing groups.

- ** Suggestion 12 **: Rule 12's pattern `['[c][OX2][C;X4][OX2]']` should be checked to ensure it captures aromatic rings with methoxy or ethoxy groups accurately. The current pattern might not enforce the presence of these specific groups.

- ** Suggestion 13 **: For Rule 13, the pattern `['[c][CX3H]=O']` should be refined to ensure it captures formyl groups on an aromatic ring without additional electron-donating groups. The current pattern might not enforce the absence of electron-donating groups.

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[c][OX2H]', '[c][NX3H2]'],  # Rule 1: Carboxylic acid and aromatic ring with electron-donating groups
        ['[NX3H2]', '[C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4]'],  # Rule 2: Amino group and linear aliphatic chain
        ['[OX2H]', '[c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 3: Hydroxyl group and aromatic ring with electron-donating groups
        ['[OX2][C;X4][OX2]'],  # Rule 4: Multiple ether linkages
        ['[SX2H]', '[C;X4][C;X4][C;X4]'],  # Rule 5: Sulfanyl group with short aliphatic chain
        ['[NX3+](=O)[O-]', '[c]'],  # Rule 6: Nitro group on an aromatic ring
        ['c1c[nH]c2c1cccc2'],  # Rule 7: Indole group
        ['c1ccncc1'],  # Rule 8: Pyridine ring
        ['[c][SX4](=O)(=O)', '[c][CX3](=O)'],  # Rule 9: Aromatic ring with sulfonyl or carbonyl groups
        ['[C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4]'],  # Rule 10: Long aliphatic chain
        ['c1ccncc1', '[c][CX3](=O)'],  # Rule 11: Pyridine ring with electron-withdrawing groups
        ['[c][OX2][C;X4][OX2]'],  # Rule 12: Aromatic ring with methoxy or ethoxy groups
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 13: Formyl group on an aromatic ring
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 4, 5, 6, 7, 12]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Rules with low prediction
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

Current rules:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing a carboxylic acid group (-COOH) and an aromatic ring with electron-donating substituents (e.g., -OH, -NH2) tend to result in a high yield. These groups enhance coordination with the metal center, stabilizing the catalyst. Examples include 4-aminobenzoic acid and 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with an amino group (-NH2) and a linear aliphatic chain of 4 to 6 carbons, without additional electron-withdrawing groups, tend to result in a high yield. The amino group enhances coordination, while the aliphatic chain provides steric effects that favor the reaction. Examples include 5-aminopentanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a hydroxyl group (-OH) and an aromatic ring with additional electron-donating groups tend to result in a high yield. The hydroxyl group participates in hydrogen bonding, stabilizing the catalyst structure. Examples include 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple ether linkages (-O-) and no additional functional groups tend to result in a low yield. The flexibility and decreased rigidity of the catalyst structure negatively impact the reaction. Examples include 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers containing a sulfanyl group (-SH) with a short aliphatic chain (up to 3 carbons) tend to result in a high yield. The sulfanyl group provides strong coordination with the metal center, enhancing catalytic activity. Examples include 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a nitro group (-NO2) on an aromatic ring tend to result in a high yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the nitro group stabilizes the metal center, enhancing the reaction. An example is 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers containing an indole group tend to result in a high yield. The indole group provides π-π interactions and additional coordination sites, enhancing the stability and reactivity of the catalyst. An example is (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring coordinates with the metal center, enhancing catalytic activity. Examples include pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with an aromatic ring and electron-withdrawing groups such as sulfonyl (-SO2-) or carbonyl (-C=O) groups tend to result in a low yield. These groups may destabilize the metal center. Examples include 4-sulfanylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with a long aliphatic chain (more than 6 carbons) without additional functional groups tend to result in a low yield. The lack of functional groups may reduce coordination with the metal center. An example is octanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers containing a pyridine ring with electron-withdrawing substituents tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature reduces the electron density on the nitrogen, affecting coordination. An example is 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with an aromatic ring and electron-donating groups such as methoxy (-OCH3) or ethoxy (-OC2H5) tend to result in a high yield. These groups enhance the electron density on the aromatic ring, stabilizing the metal center. An example is 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a formyl group (-CHO) on an aromatic ring without additional electron-donating groups tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the formyl group destabilizes the metal center. An example is 4-formylbenzoic acid.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

### Performance Evaluation of Current Rules

1. **Effectiveness of Current Rules:**
   - The current rules seem to be struggling with effectiveness, as indicated by the low validation accuracy of 0.4286. This is a significant drop from previous iterations, where accuracies were generally higher, reaching up to 0.6857 in some cases. This suggests that the rules may not be capturing the underlying patterns in the data effectively.

2. **Overfitting/Underfitting Assessment:**
   - The significant drop in validation accuracy suggests potential overfitting to the training data. The model might be capturing noise rather than the true signal, leading to poor generalization on unseen data. The consistent low accuracy across multiple iterations indicates that the rules might not be flexible enough to adapt to different data distributions.

3. **Discrepancies Analysis:**
   - For molecules where the predicted loading is high but the experimental value is low, rules with high positive SHAP values are likely problematic. For instance, Rule 7 and Rule 10 often have high positive SHAP values in such cases, indicating they might be overestimating the loading.
   - Conversely, for molecules where the predicted loading is low but the experimental value is high, rules with high negative SHAP values are likely problematic. Rules like Rule 2 and Rule 8 frequently show negative SHAP values, suggesting they might be underestimating the loading.

4. **Accuracy Improvements Interpretation:**
   - The current accuracy metrics suggest limited probability of improvement with the existing rules. The model's performance has not shown consistent improvement across iterations, indicating that the rules may need significant refinement or reevaluation.

5. **Insights from SHAP Analysis:**
   - SHAP analysis indicates that certain rules consistently contribute to incorrect predictions. For example, Rule 7 and Rule 10 often have high positive SHAP values for overestimated loadings, while Rule 2 and Rule 8 have high negative SHAP values for underestimated loadings. This suggests these rules might need adjustment to better capture the true relationship between features and outcomes.

### Recommendations for Improvement

1. **Refine Overestimated Loading Rules:**
   - Rules like Rule 7 (indole group) and Rule 10 (long aliphatic chain) should be revisited. Consider incorporating additional conditions or constraints to prevent overestimation, such as considering the presence of other functional groups that might mitigate the effect of these features.

2. **Adjust Underestimated Loading Rules:**
   - Rules like Rule 2 (amino group with aliphatic chain) and Rule 8 (pyridine ring) should be adjusted to better capture cases where these features lead to high loading. This might involve relaxing some constraints or considering interactions with other features that enhance their effect.

3. **Improve Generalization:**
   - To address overfitting, consider simplifying some rules or combining them to reduce complexity. This could help the model generalize better to unseen data by focusing on more robust patterns.

4. **Iterative Refinement Using SHAP Insights:**
   - Use SHAP analysis to iteratively refine rules. For example, if a rule consistently shows high SHAP values for incorrect predictions, investigate the conditions under which this occurs and adjust the rule accordingly. This iterative process can help fine-tune the rules to better align with the data.

5. **Incorporate Additional Features:**
   - Consider incorporating additional features or modifying existing ones based on domain knowledge. This could involve exploring new chemical properties or interactions that might influence catalyst loading, providing a more comprehensive feature set for the model to learn from.

    **Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing a carboxylic acid group (-COOH) and an aromatic ring with electron-donating substituents (e.g., -OH, -NH2) tend to result in a high yield. These groups enhance coordination with the metal center, stabilizing the catalyst. Examples include 4-aminobenzoic acid and 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with an amino group (-NH2) and a linear aliphatic chain of 4 to 6 carbons, without additional electron-withdrawing groups, tend to result in a high yield. The amino group enhances coordination, while the aliphatic chain provides steric effects that favor the reaction. Examples include 5-aminopentanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a hydroxyl group (-OH) and an aromatic ring with additional electron-donating groups tend to result in a high yield. The hydroxyl group participates in hydrogen bonding, stabilizing the catalyst structure. Examples include 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple ether linkages (-O-) and no additional functional groups tend to result in a low yield. The flexibility and decreased rigidity of the catalyst structure negatively impact the reaction. Examples include 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers containing a sulfanyl group (-SH) with a short aliphatic chain (up to 3 carbons) tend to result in a high yield. The sulfanyl group provides strong coordination with the metal center, enhancing catalytic activity. Examples include 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a nitro group (-NO2) on an aromatic ring tend to result in a high yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the nitro group stabilizes the metal center, enhancing the reaction. An example is 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers containing an indole group tend to result in a high yield. The indole group provides π-π interactions and additional coordination sites, enhancing the stability and reactivity of the catalyst. An example is (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring coordinates with the metal center, enhancing catalytic activity. Examples include pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with an aromatic ring and electron-withdrawing groups such as sulfonyl (-SO2-) or carbonyl (-C=O) groups tend to result in a low yield. These groups may destabilize the metal center. Examples include 4-sulfanylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with a long aliphatic chain (more than 6 carbons) without additional functional groups tend to result in a low yield. The lack of functional groups may reduce coordination with the metal center. An example is octanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers containing a pyridine ring with electron-withdrawing substituents tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature reduces the electron density on the nitrogen, affecting coordination. An example is 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with an aromatic ring and electron-donating groups such as methoxy (-OCH3) or ethoxy (-OC2H5) tend to result in a high yield. These groups enhance the electron density on the aromatic ring, stabilizing the metal center. An example is 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a formyl group (-CHO) on an aromatic ring without additional electron-donating groups tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the formyl group destabilizes the metal center. An example is 4-formylbenzoic acid.
